Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

---

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.
Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

---

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

---

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

### Backend (Spring Boot)

- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth

- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

---

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

---

## RxPharma — Pharmacy Management System

### What It Is

RxPharma is a full-stack web application designed to manage the day-to-day operations of a pharmacy. It covers everything from drug inventory and supplier relationships to patient prescriptions, sales, and user access control. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

---

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. The project is split into two sub-applications: a Java backend and a React frontend.

### Project Structure

The repository has three top-level areas:

- `rxpharma-backend/` — the Spring Boot REST API
- `rxpharma-frontend/` — the React + Vite single-page application
- `.github/workflows/` — CI/CD pipeline configuration

---

### Backend (Spring Boot)

**Language & Framework:** Java 21 with Spring Boot 3.4.5

The backend follows a classic layered architecture:

**Controllers** handle incoming HTTP requests and map them to service calls. There are eight controllers:
- `AuthController` — login, registration, forgot/reset password, Google OAuth
- `DrugController` — drug inventory CRUD
- `SupplierController` — supplier management
- `PrescriptionController` — prescription lifecycle
- `SaleController` — recording and retrieving sales
- `PurchaseOrderController` — ordering stock from suppliers
- `UserController` — user administration
- `DashboardController` — summary statistics for the home screen

**Services** contain the business logic. For example, `DrugService` checks stock levels and expiry dates, `PrescriptionService` handles dispensing and cancellation workflows, `SaleService` manages invoices and deducts stock, and `AuthService` handles JWT generation, BCrypt password hashing, and password reset token lifecycle (tokens expire after 30 minutes).

**Entities (Database Models):** The core domain objects are:
- `User` — has a role (`ADMIN`, `PHARMACIST`, `CASHIER`, `SUPPLIER_MANAGER`) and supports both local password auth and Google OAuth (`authProvider` field). Accounts can be pending approval.
- `Drug` — tracks name, SKU, category, price, stock quantity, expiry date, and links to a supplier.
- `Supplier` — stores company name, contact info, and a status (`ACTIVE` or `ON_HOLD`).
- `Prescription` — records patient name, doctor name, issue date, dispensed-by user, and a list of drugs with dosages. Status flows through `PENDING → DISPENSED → CANCELLED`.
- `Sale` / `SaleItem` — captures individual sales transactions and line items.
- `PurchaseOrder` / `PurchaseOrderItem` — tracks orders placed to suppliers and their delivery status.
- `PasswordResetToken` — short-lived tokens for the forgot-password flow.

**Security:** Spring Security with stateless JWT sessions. Only `/api/auth/**` is publicly accessible; every other endpoint requires a valid token. Passwords are hashed with BCrypt at strength 12. Google OAuth2 token verification is also supported via the Google API Client library. CORS is configured to allow the local dev frontend and the production Railway deployment.

**Database:** PostgreSQL is used for all persistence. The schema is managed exclusively through **Flyway migrations** (10 versioned SQL files), covering table creation, seed data, and incremental additions like user approval flags and supplier address fields. JPA is set to `validate` mode, meaning it checks the schema matches the entities without modifying it — Flyway owns all schema changes.

**DTOs:** The project uses a clean separation between the API surface and internal entities, with dedicated `Request` and `Response` DTOs for every operation (e.g., `DrugRequest`, `DrugResponse`, `PrescriptionRequest`, `AuthResponse`).

**Exception Handling:** A `GlobalExceptionHandler` catches custom exceptions (`ResourceNotFoundException`, `BadRequestException`, `DuplicateResourceException`) and returns consistent JSON error responses.

---

### Frontend (React + Vite)

**Language & Libraries:** React 19, React Router 7, Axios, Tailwind CSS, and `@react-oauth/google` for Google Sign-In.

**Pages (one per major feature):**
- `LoginPage` — email/password login and Google OAuth button
- `ForgotPasswordPage` — password reset flow
- `DashboardPage` — operational summary metrics (stock alerts, sales figures, etc.)
- `DrugsPage` — full drug inventory management
- `SuppliersPage` — supplier CRUD
- `PrescriptionsPage` — creating and managing prescriptions
- `SalesPage` — recording sales, viewing history
- `PrescriptionInvoicePage` — generating invoice documents from prescriptions
- `PurchaseOrdersPage` — managing supplier orders and deliveries
- `UsersPage` — admin-only user management and role assignment

**Routing & Access Control:** `AppRouter.jsx` defines all routes. Each protected route wraps in a `ProtectedRoute` component that checks both authentication and role. For instance, `/prescriptions` is only accessible to `ADMIN` and `PHARMACIST`; `/sales` to `ADMIN` and `CASHIER`; `/users` exclusively to `ADMIN`.

**API Layer:** A dedicated `api/` folder holds one file per backend module (e.g., `drugApi.js`, `prescriptionApi.js`). They all use a shared `axios.js` instance that automatically attaches the JWT token from local storage to every request.

**Auth State:** An `AuthContext` (React Context API) holds the logged-in user's info and provides it throughout the app.

**Styling:** Tailwind CSS with a custom config and PostCSS. The UI includes a `Sidebar`, `Navbar`, and `DashboardLayout` wrapper.

---

### DevOps & Deployment

**Docker:** Both the backend and frontend have `Dockerfile`s. The backend uses a multi-stage Maven build; the frontend uses a multi-stage Node build served via Nginx.

**CI/CD (GitHub Actions):** A `deploy.yml` pipeline triggers on every push to `main`. It runs three parallel-then-sequential jobs:
1. **Backend job** — builds with Maven, runs tests, builds and pushes a Docker image to GitHub Container Registry (GHCR).
2. **Frontend job** — installs dependencies, builds with Vite (injecting production environment variables from GitHub Secrets), and pushes a Docker image to GHCR.
3. **Deploy job** — runs after both succeed and deploys both services to **Railway** using the Railway CLI.

**Configuration:** Environment variables govern database connection, JWT secret, Google OAuth Client ID, and server port. An `.env.example` documents what needs to be set.

---

### Summary of User Roles

| Role | Access |
|---|---|
| `ADMIN` | Everything — full access to all modules |
| `PHARMACIST` | Drugs and Prescriptions |
| `CASHIER` | Drugs, Sales, and Prescription Invoices |
| `SUPPLIER_MANAGER` | Suppliers and Purchase Orders |

---

In short, RxPharma is a well-structured, production-grade pharmacy management system with proper security, clean separation of concerns, versioned database migrations, role-based access control, and a fully automated deployment pipeline.Now I have a thorough understanding of the entire project. Here's a detailed explanation:

---
